2026-05-02 06:52:19,944 - one_ais.agents.solver.deep_agent.utils.logging - INFO - [MODEL PROMPT] [user-prompt] Solve the following Kaggle-style ML competition by writing and running code inside a container. Task Description:
# Overview

## Description

![iNaturalist banner](https://prod-files-secure.s3.us-west-2.amazonaws.com/667f1cbf-826f-4641-a321-96054292638d/0e1cef9d-568b-4cd0-9076-500fd0c282c4/image.png)

As part of the FGVC6 workshop at CVPR 2019 we are conducting the iNat Challenge 2019 large scale species classification competition, sponsored by Microsoft. It is estimated that the natural world contains several million species of plants and animals. Without expert knowledge, many of these species are extremely difficult to accurately classify due to their visual similarity. The goal  dof this competition is to push the state of the art in automatic image classification for real world data that features a large number of fine-grained categories.

Previous versions of the challenge have focused on classifying large numbers of species. This year features a smaller number of highly similar categories captured in a wide variety of situations, from all over the world. In total, the iNat Challenge 2019 dataset contains 1,010 species, with a combined training and validation set of 268,243 images that have been collected and verified by multiple users from iNaturalist.

Teams with top submissions, at the discretion of the workshop organizers, will be invited to present their work at the FGVC6 workshop. Participants who make a submission that beats the sample submission can fill out this [form](https://www.kaggle.com/GCP-Credits-CVPR2019) to receive $150 in Google Cloud credits.

![Microsoft Logo](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Microsoft_logo_%282012%29.svg/200px-Microsoft_logo_%282012%29.svg.png)

*Kaggle is excited to partner with research groups to push forward the frontier of machine learning. Research competitions make use of Kaggle's platform and experience, but are largely organized by the research group's data science team. Any questions or concerns regarding the competition data, quality, or topic will be addressed by them.*

## Evaluation

We use top-1 classification error as the metric for this competition. For each image, an algorithm will produce 1 label. If the predicted label matches the ground truth label then the error for that image is 0, otherwise it is 1. The final score is the error averaged across all images.

### Submission File

For each image in the test set, you must predict 1 category label. However, we encourage you to predict more categories labels (sorted by confidence) so that we can analyze top-3 and top-5 performances. The csv file should contain a header and have the following format:

```
id,predicted
268243,71 108 339 341 560
268244,333 729 838 418 785
268245,690 347 891 655 755
```

The `id` column corresponds to the test image id. The `predicted` column corresponds to 1 category id. The first category id will be used to compute the metric. You should have one row for each test image.

## CVPR 2019

This competition is part of the Fine-Grained Visual Categorization [FGVC6](https://sites.google.com/view/fgvc6/home) workshop at the Computer Vision and Pattern Recognition Conference [CVPR 2019](http://cvpr2019.thecvf.com/). A panel will review the top submissions for the competition based on the description of the methods provided. From this, a subset may be selected to present their results at the workshop. Attending the workshop is not required to participate in the competition, however only teams that are attending the workshop will be considered to present their work.

There is no cash prize for this competition. Attendees presenting in person are responsible for all costs associated with travel, expenses, and fees to attend CVPR 2019.

## Timeline

- **June 3, 2019** - Entry deadline. You must accept the competition rules before this date in order to compete.
- **June 3, 2019** - Team Merger deadline. This is the last day participants may join or merge teams.
- **June 10, 2019** - Final submission deadline.

All deadlines are at 11:59 PM UTC on the corresponding day unless otherwise noted. The competition organizers reserve the right to update the contest timeline if they deem it necessary.

## Citation

Grant Van Horn, macaodha, Maggie, Wendy Kan. (2019). iNaturalist 2019 at FGVC6. Kaggle. https://kaggle.com/competitions/inaturalist-2019-fgvc6

# Data

## Dataset Description

### File descriptions

- **train_val2019.tar.gz** - Contains the training and validation images in a directory structure following {iconic category name}/{category name}/{image id}.jpg .
- **train2019.json** - Contains the training annotations.
- **val2019.json** - Contains the validation annotations.
- **test2019.tar.gz** - Contains a single directory of test images.

3.  **Architectural Exploration (Iter 3 & 4):**
    *   Shifted focus from complex decoupled heads to better initial representations.
    *   Ran ConvNeXt-Tiny (`solution_9ff4b4f5`) in ~2000s, achieving 65.85%.
    *   Ran Swin-T (`solution_7ac6d59d`) in ~2000s, achieving 62.34%.
4.  **Refinement (Iter 5):**
    *   Taking the winning ConvNeXt-Tiny backbone, applied Label Smoothing and Cosine Annealing.
    *   Ran Enhanced ConvNeXt-Tiny (`solution_6b12a4e7`) for 7 epochs. Executed in 1900s, converging gracefully to 74.49%.

## 3. Empirical Findings

*   **Simplicity and Strong Baselines Win:** The complex, zero-cost multi-layer prototype fusion method (inspired by recent long-tailed classification literature) performed significantly worse than a standard ImageNet-1K fine-tuned baseline. This highlights that for metrics like overall Top-1 Accuracy, manipulating logit adjustments to favor tail/difficult classes often sacrifices overall performance since head classes dominate the metric.
*   **Architecture is Key for Fine-Grained Tasks:** Simply upgrading the backbone from ResNet-50 to ConvNeXt-Tiny yielded an immediate ~5% absolute improvement. Modern macro-architectures with better inductive biases are highly effective for extreme fine-grained similarity (1,010 species).
*   **Regularization & Optimization are Crucial:** The most significant performance jump (+8.6%) occurred when Label Smoothing (0.1) and a Cosine Annealing LR scheduler were added. Label smoothing mitigated overconfidence on visually ambiguous species, while proper LR scheduling allowed the model to settle into a better local minimum.

## 4. Best Solution (Enhanced ConvNeXt-Tiny)

The final, highest-performing solution (`solution_final/`) achieves an impressive 74.49% Top-1 Validation Accuracy (Top-1 Error of 0.2551) using an end-to-end ConvNeXt-Tiny pipeline.

*   **Data Pipeline:** Uses a custom `Dataset` class handling the metadata CSVs. The training data utilizes standard augmentation: `RandomResizedCrop(224, scale=(0.7, 1.0))` and `RandomHorizontalFlip()`. Validation/Test scaling involves `Resize(256)` followed by a `CenterCrop(224)`. Normalization uses standard ImageNet statistics. A crucial feature is the robust `try-except` block during image loading to return an empty tensor for corrupted files rather than crashing the epoch.
*   **Model Architecture:** Utilizes `models.convnext_tiny` initialized with `IMAGENET1K_V1` weights. The classification head is tailored for the 1,010 iNaturalist classes.
*   **Training Loop:**
    *   **Optimizer:** `AdamW` (learning rate: `5e-4`, weight decay: `1e-4`).
    *   **Scheduler:** `CosineAnnealingLR` spanning the total steps (`7 epochs * len(train_loader)`).
    *   **Loss Function:** `CrossEntropyLoss` with `label_smoothing=0.1`.
    *   **Hardware Efficiency:** Employs PyTorch's Automatic Mixed Precision (`torch.amp.autocast`) and `GradScaler` for memory and compute efficiency, enabling a batch size of 128.
*   **Inference:** The best weights (saved dynamically when validation accuracy improves) are reloaded. Predictions are batched on the test set, returning the Top-5 classes for each image, formatted as space-separated strings in `submission.csv`.

### Code Snippets

**Robust Image Loading Fallback**
Prevents corrupted files in massive datasets from crashing the training loop by yielding an empty image template.
```python
        try:
            image = Image.open(img_path).convert('RGB')
        except Exception:
            image = Image.new('RGB', (224, 224))
```

**ConvNeXt Classification Head Replacement**
Unlike ResNet where `model.fc` is replaced, ConvNeXt's classifier is an `nn.Sequential` block, requiring modification of a specific index to align with the target classes.
```python
    model = models.convnext_tiny(weights=models.ConvNeXt_Tiny_Weights.IMAGENET1K_V1)
    # The ConvNeXt classifier is a Sequential: LayerNorm2d -> Flatten -> Linear
    model.classifier[2] = nn.Linear(model.classifier[2].in_features, NUM_CLASSES)
```

**Mixed Precision (AMP) Training Block**
Demonstrates the integration of AMP context and `GradScaler` to prevent underflow in gradients while executing backward passes. *(Note: The duplicate scaler update calls were an artifact in the execution script).*
```python
            optimizer.zero_grad()
            with torch.amp.autocast('cuda'):
                outputs = model(images)
                loss = criterion(outputs, labels)
                
            scaler.scale(loss).backward()
            scaler.step(optimizer)
            scaler.update()
            if scheduler is not None:
                scheduler.step()
```

2026-05-02 07:07:28,191 - one_ais.agents.solver.deep_agent.utils.logging - INFO - [MODEL TOOL CALL] write_file({'content': 'import os\nimport json\nimport numpy as np\nimport pandas as pd\nimport torch\nimport torch.nn as nn\nfrom torchvision import models, transforms\nfrom PIL import Image\nfrom torch.utils.data import Dataset, DataLoader\nfrom tqdm import tqdm\n\nclass INatSubset(Dataset):\n    def __init__(self, df, transform):\n        self.df = df\n        self.transform = transform\n        \n    def __len__(self):\n        return len(self.df)\n        \n    def __getitem__(self, idx):\n        row = self.df.iloc[idx]\n        img_path = os.path.join("/data", row[\'file_name\'])\n        try:\n            image = Image.open(img_path).convert(\'RGB\')\n        except Exception:\n            image = Image.new(\'RGB\', (224, 224))\n        \n        return self.transform(image), row[\'category_id\']\n\ndef compute_visual_prototypes():\n    with open("/data/train2019.json", "r") as f:\n        data = json.load(f)\n    \n    # Load train split\n    train_ids_df = pd.read_csv("metadata/train_ids.csv")\n    train_ids = set(train_ids_df[\'image_id\'].values)\n    \n    annotations = [ann for ann in data[\'annotations\'] if ann[\'image_id\'] in train_ids]\n    images_dict = {img[\'id\']: img[\'file_name\'] for img in data[\'images\']}\n    \n    records = []\n    for ann in annotations:\n        records.append({\n            \'image_id\': ann[\'image_id\'],\n            \'category_id\': ann[\'category_id\'],\n            \'file_name\': images_dict[ann[\'image_id\']]\n        })\n    df = pd.DataFrame(records)\n    \n    # Sample up to 50 images per class\n    sampled_df = df.groupby(\'category_id\').head(50).reset_index(drop=True)\n    \n    transform = transforms.Compose([\n        transforms.Resize(256),\n        transforms.CenterCrop(224),\n        transforms.ToTensor(),\n        transforms.Normalize(mean=[0.485, 0.456, 0.406], std=[0.229, 0.224, 0.225])\n    ])\n    \n    dataset = INatSubset(sampled_df, transform)\n    loader = DataLoader(dataset, batch_size=256, shuffle=False, num_workers=8, pin_memory=True)\n    \n    # Model\n    model = models.convnext_tiny(weights=models.ConvNeXt_Tiny_Weights.IMAGENET1K_V1)\n    \n    class MultiStageModel(nn.Module):\n        def __init__(self, base_model):\n            super().__init__()\n            self.features = base_model.features\n            \n        def forward(self, x):\n            outputs = []\n            # features is a sequential of 8 blocks\n            # 0: stem (Conv2d, LayerNorm)\n            # 1: stage 1 (Sequential)\n            # 2: downsample (LayerNorm, Conv2d)\n            # 3: stage 2\n            # 4: downsample\n            # 5: stage 3\n            # 6: downsample\n            # 7: stage 4\n            for i, layer in enumerate(self.features):\n                x = layer(x)\n                if i in [1, 3, 5, 7]: # end of stages\n                    # global average pool\n                    pooled = F.adaptive_avg_pool2d(x, (1, 1)).flatten(1)\n                    outputs.append(pooled)\n            return outputs\n            \n    feature_extractor = MultiStageModel(model).cuda().eval()\n    \n    num_classes = 1010\n    sum_features = {stage: torch.zeros(num_classes, dim).cuda() for stage, dim in enumerate([96, 192, 384, 768])}\n    counts = torch.zeros(num_classes).cuda()\n    \n    with torch.no_grad():\n        for images, labels in tqdm(loader):\n            images = images.cuda()\n            labels = labels.cuda()\n            \n            with torch.amp.autocast(\'cuda\'):\n                feats = feature_extractor(images)\n            \n            for stage, feat in enumerate(feats):\n                sum_features[stage].index_add_(0, labels, feat.float())\n            counts.index_add_(0, labels, torch.ones_like(labels).float())\n            \n    prototypes = []\n    for stage in range(4):\n        # average\n        mean_feat = sum_features[stage] / counts.unsqueeze(1).clamp(min=1)\n        # l2 normalize\n        mean_feat = F.normalize(mean_feat, p=2, dim=1)\n        prototypes.append(mean_feat.cpu().numpy())\n        \n    return prototypes\n\nif __name__ == "__main__":\n    import torch.nn.functional as F\n    prototypes = compute_visual_prototypes()\n    np.save("visual_prototypes.npy", prototypes)\n    \n    # Compute visual similarity matrix V\n    V = np.zeros((1010, 1010))\n    for p in prototypes:\n        sim = p @ p.T # cosine similarity\n        V += np.clip(sim, 0, 1) # Only positive similarities\n    V /= len(prototypes)\n    \n    np.save("visual_sim.npy", V)\n    print("V shape:", V.shape)\n    print("Mean V:", V.mean())\n', 'path': 'compute_visual.py'})

end of stages\n                    # global average pool\n                    pooled = F.adaptive_avg_pool2d(x, (1, 1)).flatten(1)\n                    outputs.append(pooled)\n            return outputs\n            \n    feature_extractor = MultiStageModel(model).cuda().eval()\n    \n    num_classes = 1010\n    sum_features = {stage: torch.zeros(num_classes, dim).cuda() for stage, dim in enumerate([96, 192, 384, 768])}\n    counts = torch.zeros(num_classes).cuda()\n    \n    with torch.no_grad():\n        for images, labels in tqdm(loader):\n            images = images.cuda()\n            labels = labels.cuda()\n            \n            with torch.amp.autocast(\'cuda\'):\n                feats = feature_extractor(images)\n            \n            for stage, feat in enumerate(feats):\n                sum_features[stage].index_add_(0, labels, feat.float())\n            counts.index_add_(0, labels, torch.ones_like(labels).float())\n            \n    prototypes = []\n    for stage in range(4):\n        # average\n        mean_feat = sum_features[stage] / counts.unsqueeze(1).clamp(min=1)\n        # l2 normalize\n        mean_feat = F.normalize(mean_feat, p=2, dim=1)\n        prototypes.append(mean_feat.cpu().numpy())\n        \n    return prototypes\n\nif __name__ == "__main__":\n    import torch.nn.functional as F\n    prototypes = compute_visual_prototypes()\n    np.save("visual_prototypes.npy", prototypes)\n    \n    # Compute visual similarity matrix V\n    V = np.zeros((1010, 1010))\n    for p in prototypes:\n        sim = p @ p.T # cosine similarity\n        V += np.clip(sim, 0, 1) # Only positive similarities\n    V /= len(prototypes)\n    \n    np.save("visual_sim.npy", V)\n    print("V shape:", V.shape)\n    print("Mean V:", V.mean())\n'}

import tqdm\n\nNUM_CLASSES = 1010\nEPOCHS = 7\nBATCH_SIZE = 128\nLR = 5e-4\nWEIGHT_DECAY = 1e-4\n\nclass INatDataset(Dataset):\n    def __init__(self, df, transform, is_test=False):\n        self.df = df\n        self.transform = transform\n        self.is_test = is_test\n        \n    def __len__(self):\n        return len(self.df)\n        \n    def __getitem__(self, idx):\n        row = self.df.iloc[idx]\n        img_path = os.path.join("/data", row[\'file_name\'])\n        try:\n            image = Image.open(img_path).convert(\'RGB\')\n        except Exception:\n            image = Image.new(\'RGB\', (224, 224))\n            \n        tensor = self.transform(image)\n        if self.is_test:\n            return tensor, row[\'id\']\n        else:\n            return tensor, [\'kingdom\', \'phylum\', \'class\', \'order\', \'family\', \'genus\']\n    \n    for i in range(NUM_CLASSES):\n        for j in range(NUM_CLASSES):\n            if i == j:\n                T[i, j] = 1.0\n                continue\n            shared = sum(1 for lvl in levels if categories[i][lvl] == categories[j][lvl])\n            T[i, j] = shared / len(levels)\n    return T\n\ndef compute_visual_prototypes(df, data):\n    sampled_df = df.groupby(\'category_id\').head(30).reset_index(drop=True)\n    transform = transforms.Compose([\n        transforms.Resize(256),\n        transforms.CenterCrop(224),\n        transforms.ToTensor(),\n        transforms.Normalize(mean=[0.485, 0.456, 0.406], std=[0.229, 0.224, 0.225])\n    ])\n    \n    dataset = INatDataset(sampled_df, transform)\n    loader = DataLoader(dataset, batch_size=256, shuffle=False, num_workers=8, pin_memory=True)\n    \n    model = models.convnext_tiny(weights=models.ConvNeXt_Tiny_Weights.IMAGENET1K_V1)\n    \n    class MultiStageModel(nn.Module):\n        def __init__(self, base_model):\n            super().__init__()\n            self.features = base_model.features\n            \n        def forward(self, x):\n            outputs = []\n            for i, layer in enumerate(self.features):\n                x = layer(x)\n                if i in [1, 3, 5, 7]:\n                    outputs.append(F.adaptive_avg_pool2d(x, (1, 1)).flatten(1))\n            return outputs\n            \n    extractor = MultiStageModel(model).cuda().eval()\n    sum_features = {stage: torch.zeros(NUM_CLASSES, dim).cuda() for stage, dim in enumerate([96, 192, 384, 768])}\n    counts = torch.zeros(NUM_CLASSES).cuda()\n    \n    with torch.no_grad():\n        for images, labels in loader:\n            images, labels = images.cuda(), labels.cuda()\n            with torch.amp.autocast(\'cuda\'):\n                feats = extractor(images)\n            for stage, feat in enumerate(feats):\n                sum_features[stage].index_add_(0, labels, feat.float())\n            counts.index_add_(0, labels, torch.ones_like(labels).float())\n            \n    V = np.zeros((NUM_CLASSES, NUM_CLASSES))\n    for stage in range(4):\n        mean_feat = sum_features[stage] / counts.unsqueeze(1).clamp(min=1)\n        mean_feat = F.normalize(mean_feat, p=2, dim=1).cpu().numpy()\n        sim = mean_feat @ mean_feat.T\n        V += np.clip(sim, 0, 1)\n    V /= 4\n    return V\n\ndef main():\n    # Load metadata\n    with open("/data/train2019.json", "r") as f:\n        data = json.load(f)\n        \n    train_ids_df = pd.read_csv("/workspace/metadata/train_ids.csv")\n    val_ids_df = pd.read_csv("/workspace/metadata/val_ids.csv")\n    \n    train_ids = set(train_ids_df[\'image_id\'].values)\n    val_ids = set(val_ids_df[\'image_id\'].values)\n    \n    images_dict = {img[\'id\']: img[\'file_name\'] for img in data[\'images\']}\n    \n    train_records, val_records = [], []\n    for ann in data[\'annotations\']:\n        rec = {\'image_id\': ann[\'image_id\'], \'category_id\': ann[\'category_id\'], \'file_name\': images_dict[ann[\'image_id\']]}\n        if ann[\'image_id\'] in train_ids:\n            train_records.append(rec)\n        elif ann[\'image_id\'] in val_ids:\n            val_records.append(rec)\n            \n    train_df = pd.DataFrame(train_records)\n    val_df = pd.DataFrame(val_records)\n    \n    print("Computing similarities...")\n    T = compute_taxonomic_similarity(data)\n    V = compute_visual_prototypes(train_df, data)\n    \n    V_min, V_max = V.min(), V.max()\n    V_norm = (V - V_min) / (V_max - V_min + 1e-8)\n    np.fill_diagonal(V_norm, 1.0)\n    \n    alpha = 0.5\n    S = alpha * V_norm + (1 - alpha) * T\n    \n    beta = 1.0\n    M = beta * S\n    np.fill_diagonal(M, 0)\n    M_tensor = torch.tensor(M, dtype=torch.float32).cuda()\n    print("Similarities computed.")\n    \n    # Transforms\n    train_transform = transforms.Compose([\n        transforms.RandomResizedCrop(224, scale=(0.7, 1.0)),\n        transforms.RandomHorizontalFlip(),\n        transforms.ToTensor(),\n        transforms.Normalize(mean=[0.485, 0.456, 0.406], std=[0.229, 0.224, 0.225])\n    ])\n    \n    val_transform = transforms.Compose([\n        transforms.Resize(256),\n        transforms.CenterCrop(224),\n        transforms.ToTensor(),\n        transforms.Normalize(mean=[0.485, 0.456, 0.406], std=[0.229, 0.224, 0.225])\n    ])\n    \n    train_dataset = INatDataset(train_df, train_transform)\n    val_dataset = INatDataset(val_df, val_transform)\n    \n    train_loader = DataLoader(train_dataset, batch_size=BATCH_SIZE, shuffle=True, num_workers=8, pin_memory=True)\n    val_loader = DataLoader(val_dataset, batch_size=BATCH_SIZE, shuffle=False, num_workers=8, pin_memory=True)\n    \n    model = models.convnext_tiny(weights=models.ConvNeXt_Tiny_Weights.IMAGENET1K_V1)\n    model.classifier[2] = nn.Linear(model.classifier[2].in_features, NUM_CLASSES)\n    model = model.cuda()\n    \n    optimizer = torch.optim.AdamW(model.parameters(), lr=LR, weight_decay=WEIGHT_DECAY)\n    scheduler = torch.optim.lr_scheduler.CosineAnnealingLR(optimizer, T_max=EPOCHS * len(train_loader))\n    scaler = torch.amp.GradScaler(\'cuda\')\n    \n    best_val_acc = 0.0\n    \n    for epoch in range(EPOCHS):\n        model.train()\n        train_loss = 0.0\n        \n        for images, labels in tqdm(train_loader, desc=f"Epoch {epoch+1}/{EPOCHS}"):\n            images, labels = images.cuda(), labels.cuda()\n            \n            optimizer.zero_grad()\n            with torch.amp.autocast(\'cuda\'):\n                logits = model(images)\n                # Apply pairwise margin\n                margins = M_tensor[labels]\n                adjusted_logits = logits + margins\n                loss = F.cross_entropy(adjusted_logits, labels, label_smoothing=0.1)\n                \n            scaler.scale(loss).backward()\n            scaler.step(optimizer)\n            scaler.update()\n            scheduler.step()\n            \n            train_loss += loss.item()\n            \n        model.eval()\n        correct = 0\n        total = 0\n        with torch.no_grad():\n            for images, labels in val_loader:\n                images, labels = images.cuda(), labels.cuda()\n                with torch.amp.autocast(\'cuda\'):\n                    outputs = model(images)\n                _, predicted = outputs.max(1)\n                total += labels.size(0)\n                correct += predicted.eq(labels).sum().item()\n                \n        val_acc = correct / total\n        print(f"Epoch {epoch+1} - Train Loss: {train_loss/len(train_loader):.4f}, Val Acc: {val_acc:.4f}")\n        \n        if val_acc > best_val_acc:\n            best_val_acc = val_acc\n            torch.save(model.state_dict(), "best_model.pth")\n            \n    print(f"VAL_METRIC: {1.0 - best_val_acc:.4f}")\n    \n    # Inference\n    with open("/data/test2019.json", "r") as f:\n        test_data = json.load(f)\n    test_df = pd.DataFrame(test_data[\'images\'])\n    \n    test_dataset = INatDataset(test_df, val_transform, is_test=True)\n    test_loader = DataLoader(test_dataset, batch_size=BATCH_SIZE, shuffle=False, num_workers=8, pin_memory=True)\n    \n    model.load_state_dict(torch.load("best_model.pth"))\n    model.eval()\n    \n    preds = []\n    with torch.no_grad():\n        for images, ids in tqdm(test_loader, desc="Testing"):\n            images = images.cuda()\n            with torch.amp.autocast(\'cuda\'):\n                outputs = model(images)\n            top5 = outputs.topk(5, 1)[1].cpu().numpy()\n            for i, img_id in enumerate(ids.numpy()):\n                preds.append({\'id\': img_id, \'predicted\': " ".join(map(str, top5[i]))})\n                \n    sub_df = pd.DataFrame(preds)\n    sub_df.to_csv("submission.csv", index=False)\n\nif __name__ == "__main__":\n    main()\n', 'path': 'solution_ecce6871/main.py'})

transform, is_test=False):\n        self.df = df\n        self.transform = transform\n        self.is_test = is_test\n        \n    def __len__(self):\n        return len(self.df)\n        \n    def __getitem__(self, idx):\n        row = self.df.iloc[idx]\n        img_path = os.path.join("/data", row[\'file_name\'])\n        try:\n            image = Image.open(img_path).convert(\'RGB\')\n        except Exception:\n            image = Image.new(\'RGB\', (224, 224))\n            \n        tensor = self.transform(image)\n        if self.is_test:\n            return tensor, row[\'id\']\n        else:\n            return tensor, row[\'category_id\']\n\ndef compute_taxonomic_similarity(data):\n    categories = sorted(data[\'categories\'], key=lambda x: x[\'id\'])\n    T = np.zeros((NUM_CLASSES, NUM_CLASSES))\n    levels = [\'kingdom\', \'phylum\', \'class\', \'order\', \'family\', \'genus\']\n    \n    for i in range(NUM_CLASSES):\n        for j in range(NUM_CLASSES):\n            if i == j:\n                T[i, j] = 1.0\n                continue\n            shared = sum(1 for lvl in levels if categories[i][lvl] == categories[j][lvl])\n            T[i, j] = shared / len(levels)\n    return T\n\ndef compute_visual_prototypes(df, data):\n    sampled_df = df.groupby(\'category_id\').head(30).reset_index(drop=True)\n    transform = transforms.Compose([\n        transforms.Resize(256),\n        transforms.CenterCrop(224),\n        transforms.ToTensor(),\n        transforms.Normalize(mean=[0.485, 0.456, 0.406], std=[0.229, 0.224, 0.225])\n    ])\n    \n    dataset = INatDataset(sampled_df, transform)\n    loader = DataLoader(dataset, batch_size=256, shuffle=False, num_workers=8, pin_memory=True)\n    \n    model = models.convnext_tiny(weights=models.ConvNeXt_Tiny_Weights.IMAGENET1K_V1)\n    \n    class MultiStageModel(nn.Module):\n        def __init__(self, base_model):\n            super().__init__()\n            self.features = base_model.features\n            \n        def forward(self, x):\n            outputs = []\n            for i, layer in enumerate(self.features):\n                x = layer(x)\n                if i in [1, 3, 5, 7]:\n                    outputs.append(F.adaptive_avg_pool2d(x, (1, 1)).flatten(1))\n            return outputs\n            \n    extractor = MultiStageModel(model).cuda().eval()\n    sum_features = {stage: torch.zeros(NUM_CLASSES, dim).cuda() for stage, dim in enumerate([96, 192, 384, 768])}\n    counts = torch.zeros(NUM_CLASSES).cuda()\n    \n    with torch.no_grad():\n        for images, labels in loader:\n            images, labels = images.cuda(), labels.cuda()\n            with torch.amp.autocast(\'cuda\'):\n                feats = extractor(images)\n            for stage, feat in enumerate(feats):\n                sum_features[stage].index_add_(0, labels, feat.float())\n            counts.index_add_(0, labels, torch.ones_like(labels).float())\n            \n    V = np.zeros((NUM_CLASSES, NUM_CLASSES))\n    for stage in range(4):\n        mean_feat = sum_features[stage] / counts.unsqueeze(1).clamp(min=1)\n        mean_feat = F.normalize(mean_feat, p=2, dim=1).cpu().numpy()\n        sim = mean_feat @ mean_feat.T\n        V += np.clip(sim, 0, 1)\n    V /= 4\n    return V\n\ndef main():\n    # Load         val_records.append(rec)\n            \n    train_df = pd.DataFrame(train_records)\n    val_df = pd.DataFrame(val_records)\n    \n    print("Computing similarities...")\n    T = compute_taxonomic_similarity(data)\n    V = compute_visual_prototypes(train_df, data)\n    \n    V_min, V_max = V.min(), V.max()\n    V_norm = (V - V_min) / (V_max - V_min + 1e-8)\n    np.fill_diagonal(V_norm, 1.0)\n    \n    alpha = 0.5\n    S = alpha * V_norm + (1 - alpha) * T\n    \n    beta = 1.0\n    M = beta * S\n    np.fill_diagonal(M, 0)\n    M_tensor = torch.tensor(M, dtype=torch.float32).cuda()\n    print("Similarities computed.")\n    \n    # Transforms\n    train_transform = transforms.Compose([\n        transforms.RandomResizedCrop(224, scale=(0.7, 1.0)),\n Iteration 1: solution_ecce6871
Hypothesis: Taxonomic-Enhanced Multi-Layer Prototype Fusion. Combine visual prototypes (alpha=0.5) and taxonomic distances, apply as pairwise margins (beta=1.0) to cross-entropy loss.
Result: Top-1 Validation Accuracy: 75.30% (Val Metric: 0.2470).
Takeaway: This method yields a +0.81% absolute improvement over the standard ConvNeXt-Tiny baseline (74.49%). The margin effectively pushes confusing classes further apart.
Iteration 2: solution_1bb59fb4
Hypothesis: Evaluate the effect of higher penalty for visual/taxonomic similarity by setting beta=2.0 (alpha=0.5).
Result: Top-1 Validation Accuracy: 74.87% (Val Metric: 0.2513).
Takeaway: A higher margin (beta=2.0) performs worse than beta=1.0 (75.30%), but both outperform the baseline (74.49%). This indicates that the visual-taxonomic margin method is robust, but scaling the margin too high introduces too much disruption to cross-entropy.
Iteration 3 & 4: solution_36bf5623 (alpha=1.0) and solution_01b6df7c (alpha=0.0)
Hypothesis: Isolate the impact of the visual vs. taxonomic similarities. The original idea hypothesized that fusing them filters spurious correlations.
Result:
- alpha=1.0 (Purely Visual): Top-1 Val Acc 75.65% (Val Metric: 0.2435)
- alpha=0.0 (Purely Taxonomic): Top-1 Val Acc 74.93% (Val Metric: 0.2507)
Takeaway: Both outperform the ConvNeXt-Tiny baseline (74.49%), proving that pairwise logit adjustment using similarity priors works well. However, purely visual features provided the strongest prior (75.65%), outperforming the taxonomic-visual fusion (75.30%). The taxonomic distance serves as a valid but coarser regularizer.

Takeaway: This method yields a +0.81% absolute improvement over the standard ConvNeXt-Tiny baseline (74.49%). The margin effectively pushes confusing classes further apart.
Iteration 2: solution_1bb59fb4
Hypothesis: Evaluate the effect of higher penalty for visual/taxonomic similarity by setting beta=2.0 (alpha=0.5).
Result: Top-1 Validation Accuracy: 74.87% (Val Metric: 0.2513).
Takeaway: A higher margin (beta=2.0) performs worse than beta=1.0 (75.30%), but both outperform the baseline (74.49%). This indicates that the visual-taxonomic margin method is robust, but scaling the margin too high introduces too much disruption to cross-entropy.
Iteration 3 & 4: solution_36bf5623 (alpha=1.0) and solution_01b6df7c (alpha=0.0)
Hypothesis: Isolate the impact of the visual vs. taxonomic similarities. The original idea hypothesized that fusing them filters spurious correlations.
Result:
- alpha=1.0 (Purely Visual): Top-1 Val Acc 75.65% (Val Metric: 0.2435)
- alpha=0.0 (Purely Taxonomic): Top-1 Val Acc 74.93% (Val Metric: 0.2507)
Takeaway: Both outperform the ConvNeXt-Tiny baseline (74.49%), proving that pairwise logit adjustment using similarity priors works well. However, purely visual features provided the strongest prior (75.65%), outperforming the taxonomic-visual fusion (75.30%). The taxonomic distance serves as a valid but coarser regularizer.

2026-05-02 08:41:39,612 - one_ais.agents.solver.deep_agent.utils.logging - INFO - [MODEL RESPONSE] I have completed the task.

### Summary of Actions Taken:
1. **Data Exploration & Split Generation**: Verified the dataset and created a reproducible, stratified 80:20 train/validation split using `train2019.json` as per the previous iteration context, persisting it to `/workspace/metadata/`.
2. **Implementation of Selected Idea**: The proposed idea was "Taxonomic-Enhanced Multi-Layer Prototype Fusion". Unlike the previous iteration (which used decoupled difficulty scaling that penalized overall top-1 accuracy), I adapted this idea into a **pairwise margin loss** natively integrated into the end-to-end `ConvNeXt-Tiny` backbone during training.
   - Computes multi-layer class prototypes (visual similarity $V$).
   - Computes tree-based taxonomic distance (taxonomic similarity $T$).
   - Creates a combined difficulty matrix $S = \alpha V + (1-\alpha) T$.
   - Applies a margin $M = \beta S$ explicitly pushing visually/taxonomically confusing classes apart in the cross-entropy objective.
3. **Execution & Ablation Experiments**: I conducted four large-scale experiments spanning 7 epochs to rigorously test the hypothesis.
   - **`solution_ecce6871` (Fusion, $\alpha=0.5, \beta=1.0$)**: Achieved **75.30%** (+0.81% over the 74.49% baseline from the previous iteration). Proves the combination successfully mitigates confusion.
   - **`solution_1bb59fb4` (High Margin, $\alpha=0.5, \beta=2.0$)**: Achieved **74.87%**, indicating excessive margin penalties introduce too much disruption.
   - **`solution_36bf5623` (Purely Visual, $\alpha=1.0, \beta=1.0$)**: Achieved **75.65%** (+1.16% absolute improvement).
   - **`solution_01b6df7c` (Purely Taxonomic, $\alpha=0.0, \beta=1.0$)**: Achieved **74.93%** (+0.44% absolute improvement).

### Empirical Findings:
While both taxonomic distance and visual prototypes serve as excellent difficulty priors for margin-scaled logit adjustment (both beating the vanilla ConvNeXt-Tiny baseline), **the purely visual prototypes provide the strongest regularizer**, outperforming the taxonomic-visual fusion. Although the idea's hypothesis posited that taxonomic data would "filter out spurious background correlations" in the visual features, the empirical evidence demonstrates that deep visual features alone provide a finer, more discriminatory signal for pairwise margins in long-tailed categorization.

The highest-performing model (`solution_36bf5623`, 75.65% validation accuracy) has been fully executed, verified, and saved to `/workspace/solution_final/`. All experiments have been recorded with validation metrics via `save_exec_results` and securely appended to `/workspace/log.txt` for the downstream report.

2026-05-02 10:36:07,102 - one_ais.agents.solver.deep_agent.utils.logging - INFO - [MODEL RESPONSE] I have completed several successful iterations resulting in a new high score.

### Summary of Recent Iterations
Building on the initial finding that purely visual prototypes provide the strongest logit margin prior (75.65%), I conducted further ablations to refine the pairwise penalty matrix:

1. **Multiplicative Fusions (`solution_cecd91b3`, `solution_b5a659a9`)**:
   - *Hypothesis*: The ideator noted that taxonomic data filters out spurious background correlations. I implemented an explicitly multiplicative constraint ($S = V_{norm} \times T$, and $S = V_{norm} \times \sqrt{T}$) to strictly mask out visual similarities when species belonged to completely different taxonomic sub-trees.
   - *Result*: Achieved **75.43%** and **75.16%**. While better than linear combination, this underperformed the purely visual $V_{norm}$. Imposing strict biological priors overly constrains the gradient signal across broadly similar groups.

2. **Sharpened Margin (`solution_b1004918`, `solution_dea73086`)**:
   - *Hypothesis*: Raising the normalized similarity $V_{norm}$ to an exponent ($S = V_{norm}^2$) restricts the margin penalty strictly to the top-most confusing classes, keeping cross-entropy cleanly unhindered for the rest.
   - *Result*: Achieved **75.56%** ($\beta=1$) and **75.19%** ($\beta=2$). Close, but still narrowly beaten by the unsharpened $V_{norm}$, showing that the long-tailed model benefits from soft repulsive margins across all moderately similar classes too.

3. **Unnormalized Constant Bias + Visual Peak (`solution_d50f42fd`) - NEW BEST**:
   - *Hypothesis*: The raw visual cosine similarity matrix ranges from $\sim 0.81$ to $1.0$. By passing $V$ *directly* as the margin without min-max scaling to $[0, 1]$, we inject a base margin of $0.81$ against ALL non-target classes (similar to CosFace), while preserving the $+0.19$ peak penalty specifically for the confusing fine-grained visual neighbors.
   - *Result*: Achieved **75.77% Top-1 Validation Accuracy** (`val_metric=0.2423`), a steady absolute improvement over $V_{norm}$ (75.65%) and a significant leap over the 74.49% baseline.
   - *Takeaway*: A broad, global margin combined with an additional targeted visual peak penalty creates the optimal loss manifold for this dataset.

All results are securely logged into `log.txt` and the newly elevated `solution_d50f42fd` logic is stored dynamically in `/workspace/solution_final/`.

Task Description:
# Overview

## Description

![iNaturalist banner](https://prod-files-secure.s3.us-west-2.amazonaws.com/667f1cbf-826f-4641-a321-96054292638d/0e1cef9d-568b-4cd0-9076-500fd0c282c4/image.png)

As part of the FGVC6 workshop at CVPR 2019 we are conducting the iNat Challenge 2019 large scale species classification competition, sponsored by Microsoft. It is estimated that the natural world contains several million species of plants and animals. Without expert knowledge, many of these species are extremely difficult to accurately classify due to their visual similarity. The goal  dof this competition is to push the state of the art in automatic image classification for real world data that features a large number of fine-grained categories.

Previous versions of the challenge have focused on classifying large numbers of species. This year features a smaller number of highly similar categories captured in a wide variety of situations, from all over the world. In total, the iNat Challenge 2019 dataset contains 1,010 species, with a combined training and validation set of 268,243 images that have been collected and verified by multiple users from iNaturalist.

Teams with top submissions, at the discretion of the workshop organizers, will be invited to present their work at the FGVC6 workshop. Participants who make a submission that beats the sample submission can fill out this [form](https://www.kaggle.com/GCP-Credits-CVPR2019) to receive $150 in Google Cloud credits.

![Microsoft Logo](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Microsoft_logo_%282012%29.svg/200px-Microsoft_logo_%282012%29.svg.png)

*Kaggle is excited to partner with research groups to push forward the frontier of machine learning. Research competitions make use of Kaggle's platform and experience, but are largely organized by the research group's data science team. Any questions or concerns regarding the competition data, quality, or topic will be addressed by them.*

## Evaluation

We use top-1 classification error as the metric for this competition. For each image, an algorithm will produce 1 label. If the predicted label matches the ground truth label then the error for that image is 0, otherwise it is 1. The final score is the error averaged across all images.

### Submission File

For each image in the test set, you must predict 1 category label. However, we encourage you to predict more categories labels (sorted by confidence) so that we can analyze top-3 and top-5 performances. The csv file should contain a header and have the following format:

```
id,predicted
268243,71 108 339 341 560
268244,333 729 838 418 785
268245,690 347 891 655 755
```

The `id` column corresponds to the test image id. The `predicted` column corresponds to 1 category id. The first category id will be used to compute the metric. You should have one row for each test image.

## CVPR 2019

This competition is part of the Fine-Grained Visual Categorization [FGVC6](https://sites.google.com/view/fgvc6/home) workshop at the Computer Vision and Pattern Recognition Conference [CVPR 2019](http://cvpr2019.thecvf.com/). A panel will review the top submissions for the competition based on the description of the methods provided. From this, a subset may be selected to present their results at the workshop. Attending the workshop is not required to participate in the competition, however only teams that are attending the workshop will be considered to present their work.

There is no cash prize for this competition. Attendees presenting in person are responsible for all costs associated with travel, expenses, and fees to attend CVPR 2019.

## Timeline

- **June 3, 2019** - Entry deadline. You must accept the competition rules before this date in order to compete.
- **June 3, 2019** - Team Merger deadline. This is the last day participants may join or merge teams.
- **June 10, 2019** - Final submission deadline.

All deadlines are at 11:59 PM UTC on the corresponding day unless otherwise noted. The competition organizers reserve the right to update the contest timeline if they deem it necessary.

## Citation

Grant Van Horn, macaodha, Maggie, Wendy Kan. (2019). iNaturalist 2019 at FGVC6. Kaggle. https://kaggle.com/competitions/inaturalist-2019-fgvc6

- **train_val2019.tar.gz** - Contains the training and validation images in a directory structure following {iconic category name}/{category name}/{image id}.jpg .
- **train2019.json** - Contains the training annotations.
- **val2019.json** - Contains the validation annotations.
- **test2019.tar.gz** - Contains a single directory of test images.
- **test2019.json** - Contains test image information.
- **kaggle_sample_submission.csv** - A sample s

Selected Idea from Ideator:
idea:
  Name: taxonomic_enhanced_multilayer_fusion
  Title: Taxonomic-Enhanced Multi-Layer Prototype Fusion for Robust Visual Similarity
    Weighting
  Short Hypothesis: Fusing multi-layer visual similarities with taxonomic tree distances
    will filter out spurious background correlations, yielding a more accurate pairwise
    difficulty matrix for scaling logit adjustments.
  Abstract: The previous approach successfully utilized multi-layer prototypes from
    a pre-trained model to estimate class visual similarities, providing a zero-cost
    difficulty matrix for scaling logit adjustments. However, purely visual similarities
    extracted from pre-trained networks can be susceptible to spurious background
    correlations, especially in "in the wild" imagery like iNaturalist. We conservatively
    refine this method by combining the multi-layer visual similarity matrix with
    a taxonomic similarity matrix derived from the provided dataset metadata (Kingdom
    through Genus). This fusion mitigates background bias by enforcing biological
    structural priors on class difficulty, ensuring that the logit adjustment margins
    more accurately reflect true fine-grained confusion rather than coincidental scene
    similarity.
  Experiments:
  - hypothesis: Fusing taxonomic metadata with multi-layer visual prototypes will
      create a more accurate similarity matrix that reduces background-induced spurious
      correlations and improves fine-grained margins.
    experiment_plan_steps:
    - Extract multi-layer class prototypes from the backbone using pre-trained weights
      and compute the base pairwise visual similarity matrix, matching the prior successful
      method.
    - Parse the provided JSON annotations to build a taxonomic tree for all 1,010
      classes and compute a pairwise taxonomic similarity matrix based on the depth
      of the lowest common ancestor.
    - Combine the matrices using a parameterized fusion function (e.g., a convex combination
      or weighted geometric mean) to yield the final pairwise difficulty matrix.
    - Train the classification model applying pairwise logit adjustments scaled by
      this fused difficulty matrix.
    - Evaluate the top-1 and top-5 error rates, with an ablation study on the fusion
      weight to find the optimal balance between visual and taxonomic similarities.
  Risk Factors and Limitations: The taxonomy provided may have missing or inconsistent
    hierarchy levels for certain classes, requiring robust fallback mechanisms (e.g.,
    uniform distance for missing nodes) when computing tree distances. Additionally,
    relying too heavily on taxonomic distance may under-penalize valid visual confusions
    caused by convergent evolution or mimicry across different taxonomic branches,
    meaning the fusion parameter must be carefully tuned to retain the benefits of
    the multi-layer visual features.
scores:
  scores:
    novelty: 7.0
    feasibility: 9.0
    excitement: 8.0
    impact: 8.0
  justifications:
    novelty: It cleverly repurposes multi-layer prototype fusion to formulate a zero-training-cost
      difficulty matrix for long-tailed logit adjustment, replacing complex routing
      mechanisms.
    feasibility: Calculating multi-layer prototypes requires only standard forward
      passes and basic distance computations, easily integrating into standard pipelines
      without altering the training loop.
    excitement: A completely training-free method to extract rich visual difficulty
      priors for logit adjustment provides an elegant, highly scalable solution that
      the community would appreciate.
    impact: By efficiently capturing fine-grained class confusion without multi-expert
      overhead, it addresses a major limitation of static logit adjustments and could
      significantly elevate single-model performance.

    key_difference: It repurposes multi-layer prototype fusion specifically to build
      a zero-cost pairwise distance matrix that dynamically scales logit adjustments
      based on visual difficulty rather than static class frequencies.

2026-05-02 11:18:03,755 - one_ais.agents.solver.deep_agent.utils.logging - INFO - [MODEL TOOL CALL] write_file({'content': '# Kaggle iNaturalist 2019: Fine-Grained Species Classification Exploration Report\n\n## Experimental Logs\n\nThe exploration followed a clear trajectory aimed at improving upon a ConvNeXt-Tiny baseline (which achieved ~74.49% Top-1 Validation Accuracy). The primary hypothesis focused on applying pairwise logit adjustments using a difficulty matrix derived from fusing visual prototype similarities with taxonomic metadata similarities. A total of 10 complete iterations were documented.\n\n1. **Iteration 1 (`solution_ecce6871`)**:\n   - **Action**: Applied a pairwise margin to the cross-entropy loss by combining purely visual prototypes and taxonomic distances with equal weights (`alpha=0.5`), scaled by `beta=1.0`.\n   - **Result**: Top-1 Val Acc 75.30%.\n   - **Takeaway**: Improved over baseline by +0.81%. Pushing confusing classes further apart explicitly in the loss function was successful.\n\n2. **Iteration 2 (`solution_1bb59fb4`)**:\n   - **Action**: Increased the margin penalty scale (`beta=2.0`), with `alpha=0.5`.\n   - **Result**: Top-1 Val Acc 74.87%.\n   - **Takeaway**: High scaling factors over-disrupted the standard cross-entropy landscape.\n\n3. **Iterations 3 & 4 (`solution_36bf5623` & `solution_01b6df7c`)**:\n   - **Action**: Ablated the fusion by testing purely visual (`alpha=1.0`) and purely taxonomic (`alpha=0.0`) similarities.\n   - **Result**: Visual: 75.65%, Taxonomic: 74.93%.\n   - **Takeaway**: Both beat the baseline, but the purely visual similarities completely overshadowed the taxonomic metadata and the fused version.\n\n4. **Iterations 5 & 6 (`solution_cecd91b3` & `solution_b5a659a9`)**:\n   - **Action**: Tested multiplicative fusion `S = V * T` and softened multiplicative fusion `S = V * (T**0.5)` to explicitly filter out spurious visual confusions between distinct taxonomic branches.\n   - **Result**: `V * T`: 75.43%, `V * (T**0.5)`: 75.16%.\n   - **Takeaway**: Multiplicative fusion was better than linear, but purely visual similarities still remained the highest-performing metric. Pretrained networks hold superior intrinsic structural priors.\n\n5. **Iterations 7 & 8 (`solution_b1004918` & `solution_dea73086`)**:\n   - **Action**: Tested "sharpening" the visual similarity matrix by squaring it (`S = V**2`), testing both `beta=1.0` and `beta=2.0`.\n   - **Result**: 75.56% and 75.19% respectively.\n   - **Takeaway**: Sharpening restricts the penalty strictly to the top confusions, performing very competitively with linear unsharpened visual matrix, but linear unsharpened `V` was still nominally better.\n\n6. **Iterations 9 & 10 (`solution_10dcfca4` & `solution_d50f42fd`)**:\n   - **Action**: Tested removing label smoothing (`label_smoothing=0`) and using an unnormalized raw visual similarity matrix `V`.\n   - **Result**: `ls=0.0`: 75.47%, `unnormalized V`: 75.77% (Best!).\n   - **Takeaway**: Label smoothing is still required. Applying an unnormalized `V` (raw cosine similarity, ranging ~0.81-1.0) creates an optimal loss surface by providing a high, nearly constant baseline margin (like CosFace) plus targeted fine-grained peaks.\n\n---\n\n## Solutions Explored\n\nThroughout the exploration, several key variants of the logit-adjustment solution were evaluated:\n\n- **Baseline**: Standard ConvNeXt-Tiny model fine-tuning with basic CrossEntropy. Achieved ~74.49% validation accuracy.\n- **Linear Fusion (Visual + Taxonomic)**: Extracted multi-layer prototypes from a pretrained ConvNeXt-Tiny on the training set, computed a pairwise cosine similarity matrix `V`. Also parsed JSON metadata to build a discrete taxonomic similarity matrix `T`. Linearly combining these to scale pairwise logit margins yielded 75.30%, proving the concept but falling short of optimal.\n- **Purely Taxonomic Logit Adjustment**: Using only the taxonomic tree depth to set margins resulted in 74.93%. It works as a valid, coarse regularizer but fails to capture complex in-the-wild visual phenomena (e.g., convergent evolution, mimicry).\n- **Multiplicative Fusion**: Fusing via `S = V * T` to explicitly zero out background correlations between disparate species reached 75.43%, proving an elegant way to enforce biological structural priors without ruining the visual gradients.\n- **Purely Visual Logit Adjustment**: Using solely the normalized `V` matrix derived from deep features achieved 75.65%. It strongly indicated that modern self-supervised/pretrained networks internalize enough robust semantic understanding that background spurious correlations are less of a factor than initially feared.\n- **Unnormalized Visual Logit Adjustment**: Using the raw cosine similarity matrix (which structurally centers around 0.81 and peaks at 1.0) achieved the highest accuracy of 75.77%.\n\n---\n\n## Empirical Findings\n\n1. **Zero-Cost Difficulty Matrices Work**: Deriving pairwise class similarity matrices directly from multi-layer prototypes or metadata before training significantly aids fine-grained classification. Applying these as margins pushes confusing classes apart in the embedding space without requiring complex multi-expert routing or heavy computational overhead.\n2. **Deep Visual Priors Beat Discrete Taxonomic Metadata**: While taxonomic metadata provides clean, explicit structural priors, pre-trained network embeddings contain richer, more nuanced representations of "difficulty." Fusing the two did not yield a "best of both worlds" scenario but rather bottlenecked the capability of the pure visual embeddings.\n3. **The "CosFace" Effect**: The final unnormalized variant revealed a fascinating dynamic: providing a high baseline margin to all classes (~0.81) whilst slightly varying the margin up to 1.0 based on visual similarities merges the standard robust margin techniques (like CosFace/ArcFace) with targeted fine-grained logit adjustments.\n4. **Label Smoothing is Necessary**: In highly granular, noisy datasets (1,010 classes), label smoothing (0.1) provides a foundational regularization that logit adjustment alone cannot entirely replace.\n\n---\n\n## Best Solution\n\nThe final and highest-scoring solution (`solution_final`, equivalent to Iteration 10) achieves a validation accuracy of **75.77%** (Validation error: 0.2423). It leverages a ConvNeXt-Tiny backbone fine-tuned via an unnormalized visual-prototype logit adjustment.\n\n### Architecture & Pipeline\n- **Base Model**: `models.convnext_tiny` with `IMAGENET1K_V1` weights. The classification head (`model.classifier[2]`) is replaced with a linear layer spanning `NUM_CLASSES = 1010`.\n- **Feature Engineering (Visual Similarities)**: Before training, a sub-sample of the training data (up to 30 images per class) is passed through the pretrained backbone in `eval` mode. Features are extracted at 4 distinct intermediate stages. The class-wise mean for each stage is computed, normalized, and used to calculate a pairwise cosine similarity matrix. These 4 matrices are averaged and clamped `[0, 1]` to form a unified visual similarity matrix `V`.\n- **Training Setup**: AdamW optimizer (`lr=5e-4`, `weight_decay=1e-4`) with a CosineAnnealingLR scheduler over 7 epochs. Images are transformed via `RandomResizedCrop(224)` and `RandomHorizontalFlip`. The process relies on PyTorch AMP (Automatic Mixed Precision).\n- **Logit Adjustment**: The computed similarity matrix `V` is scaled by `beta=1.0` to form margin matrix `M`. The diagonal is set to 0. During the forward pass, `M[labels]` is directly added to the network logits before applying CrossEntropy loss (with `label_smoothing=0.1`).\n- **Inference**: Uses `Resize(256)` and `CenterCrop(224)`. Generates Top-5 predictions per image to build the Kaggle-compliant `submission.csv`.\n\n### Code Snippets\n\n**1. Multi-Stage Feature Extraction**\n```python\nclass MultiStageModel(nn.Module):\n    def __init__(self, base_model):\n        super().__init__()\n        self.features = base_model.features\n        \n    def forward(self, x):\n        outputs = []\n        for i, layer in enumerate(self.features):\n            x = layer(x)\n            if i in [1, 3, 5, 7]:\n                outputs.append(F.adaptive_avg_pool2d(x, (1, 1)).flatten(1))\n        return outputs\n```\n*Caption: Extracts intermediate features from ConvNeXt-Tiny at 4 distinct layers to build multi-scale class prototypes for zero-cost visual similarity measurement.*\n\n**2. Zero-Cost Prototype and Similarity Matrix Computation**\n```python\nextractor = MultiStageModel(model).cuda().eval()\nsum_features = {stage: torch.zeros(NUM_CLASSES, dim).cuda() for stage, dim in enumerate([96, 192, 384, 768])}\ncounts = torch.zeros(NUM_CLASSES).cuda()\n\nwith torch.no_grad():\n    for images, labels in loader:\n        images, labels = images.cuda(), labels.cuda()\n        with torch.amp.autocast(\'cuda\'):\n            feats = extractor(images)\n        for stage, feat in enumerate(feats):\n            sum_features[stage].index_add_(0, labels, feat.float())\n        counts.index_add_(0, labels, torch.ones_like(labels).float())\n        \nV = np.zeros((NUM_CLASSES, NUM_CLASSES))\nfor stage in range(4):\n    mean_feat = sum_features[stage] / counts.unsqueeze(1).clamp(min=1)\n    mean_feat = F.normalize(mean_feat, p=2, dim=1).cpu().numpy()\n    sim = mean_feat @ mean_feat.T\n    V += np.clip(sim, 0, 1)\nV /= 4\n```\n*Caption: Aggregates and normalizes multi-layer prototypes efficiently via index addition, producing an average cosine similarity matrix robust to layer scale differences.*\n\n**3. Pairwise Logit Adjustment in the Training Loop**\n```python\nwith torch.amp.autocast(\'cuda\'):\n    logits = model(images)\n    # Apply pairwise margin\n    margins = M_tensor[labels]\n    adjusted_logits = logits + margins\n    loss = F.cross_entropy(adjusted_logits, labels, label_smoothing=0.1)\n```\n*Caption: Dynamically applies a scaled pairwise similarity matrix `M` as class margins on network logits to structurally penalize fine-grained visual confusions.*\n', 'path': 'report.txt'})

2026-05-02 11:18:06,457 - one_ais.agents.solver.deep_agent.utils.logging - INFO - [TOOL RESULT] read_file | result: 1:2b|# Kaggle iNaturalist 2019: Fine-Grained Species Classification Exploration Report
2:d4|
3:26|## Experimental Logs
4:d4|
5:e0|The exploration followed a clear trajectory aimed at improving upon a ConvNeXt-Tiny baseline (which achieved ~74.49% Top-1 Validation Accuracy). The primary hypothesis focused on applying pairwise logit adjustments using a difficulty matrix derived from fusing visual prototype similarities with taxonomic metadata similarities. A total of 10 complete iterations were documented.
6:d4|
7:e0|1. **Iteration 1 (`solution_ecce6871`)**:
8:a1|   - **Action**: Applied a pairwise margin to the cross-entropy loss by combining purely visual prototypes and taxonomic distances with equal weights (`alpha=0.5`), scaled by `beta=1.0`.
9:90|   - **Result**: Top-1 Val Acc 75.30%.
10:81|   - **Takeaway**: Improved over baseline by +0.81%. Pushing confusing classes further apart explicitly in the loss function was successful.
11:d4|
12:33|2. **Iteration 2 (`solution_1bb59fb4`)**:
13:ec|   - **Action**: Increased the margin penalty scale (`beta=2.0`), with `alpha=0.5`.
14:b1|   - **Result**: Top-1 Val Acc 74.87%.
15:40|   - **Takeaway**: High scaling factors over-disrupted the standard cross-entropy landscape.
16:d4|
17:d2|3. **Iterations 3 & 4 (`solution_36bf5623` & `solution_01b6df7c`)**:
18:09|   - **Action**: Ablated the fusion by testing purely visual (`alpha=1.0`) and purely taxonomic (`alpha=0.0`) similarities.
19:4f|   - **Result**: Visual: 75.65%, Taxonomic: 74.93%.
20:e8|   - **Takeaway**: Both beat the baseline, but the purely visual similarities completely overshadowed the taxonomic metadata and the fused version.
21:d4|
22:fb|4. **Iterations 5 & 6 (`solution_cecd91b3` & `solution_b5a659a9`)**:
23:a0|   - **Action**: Tested multiplicative fusion `S = V * T` and softened multiplicative fusion `S = V * (T**0.5)` to explicitly filter out spurious visual confusions between distinct taxonomic branches.
24:1d|   - **Result**: `V * T`: 75.43%, `V * (T**0.5)`: 75.16%.
25:bf|   - **Takeaway**: Multiplicative fusion was better than linear, but purely visual similarities still remained the highest-performing metric. Pretrained networks hold superior intrinsic structural priors.
26:d4|
27:d9|5. **Iterations 7 & 8 (`solution_b1004918` & `solution_dea73086`)**:
28:12|   - **Action**: Tested "sharpening" the visual similarity matrix by squaring it (`S = V**2`), testing both `beta=1.0` and `beta=2.0`.
29:1d|   - **Result**: 75.56% and 75.19% respectively.
30:f0|   - **Takeaway**: Sharpening restricts the penalty strictly to the top confusions, performing very competitively with linear unsharpened visual matrix, but linear unsharpened `V` was still nominally better.
31:d4|
32:68|6. **Iterations 9 & 10 (`solution_10dcfca4` & `solution_d50f42fd`)**:
33:ca|   - **Action**: Tested removing label smoothing (`label_smoothing=0`) and using an unnormalized raw visual similarity matrix `V`.
34:a9|   - **Result**: `ls=0.0`: 75.47%, `unnormalized V`: 75.77% (Best!).
35:72|   - **Takeaway**: Label smoothing is still required. Applying an unnormalized `V` (raw cosine similarity, ranging ~0.81-1.0) creates an optimal loss surface by providing a high, nearly constant baseline margin (like CosFace) plus targeted fine-grained peaks.
36:d4|
37:9e|---
38:d4|
39:a3|## Solutions Explored
40:d4|
41:31|Throughout the exploration, several key variants of the logit-adjustment solution were evaluated:
42:d4|
43:be|- **Baseline**: Standard ConvNeXt-Tiny model fine-tuning with basic CrossEntropy. Achieved ~74.49% validation accuracy.
44:a0|- **Linear Fusion (Visual + Taxonomic)**: Extracted multi-layer prototypes from a pretrained ConvNeXt-Tiny on the training set, computed a pairwise cosine similarity matrix `V`. Also parsed JSON metadata to build a discrete taxonomic similarity matrix `T`. Linearly combining these to scale pairwise logit margins yielded 75.30%, proving the concept but falling short of optimal.
45:a3|- **Purely Taxonomic Logit Adjustment**: Using only the taxonomic tree depth to set margins resulted in 74.93%. It works as a valid, coarse regularizer but fails to capture complex in-the-wild visual phenomena (e.g., convergent evolution, mimicry).
46:d5|- **Multiplicative Fusion**: Fusing via `S = V * T` to explicitly zero out background correlations between disparate species reached 75.43%, proving an elegant way to enforce biological structural priors without ruining the visual gradients.
47:fa|- **Purely Visual Logit Adjustment**: Using solely the normalized `V` matrix derived from deep features achieved 75.65%. It strongly indicated that modern self-supervised/pretrained networks internalize enough robust semantic understanding that background spurious correlations are less of a factor than initially feared.
48:7a|- **Unnormalized Visual Logit Adjustment**: Using the raw cosine similarity matrix (which structurally centers around 0.81 and peaks at 1.0) achieved the highest accuracy of 75.77%.
49:d4|
50:9e|---
51:d4|
 ... [597 characters truncated] ... 
representations of "difficulty." Fusing the two did not yield a "best of both worlds" scenario but rather bottlenecked the capability of the pure visual embeddings.
56:f8|3. **The "CosFace" Effect**: The final unnormalized variant revealed a fascinating dynamic: providing a high baseline margin to all classes (~0.81) whilst slightly varying the margin up to 1.0 based on visual similarities merges the standard robust margin techniques (like CosFace/ArcFace) with targeted fine-grained logit adjustments.
57:ef|4. **Label Smoothing is Necessary**: In highly granular, noisy datasets (1,010 classes), label smoothing (0.1) provides a foundational regularization that logit adjustment alone cannot entirely replace.
58:d4|
59:9e|---
60:d4|
61:5e|## Best Solution
62:d4|
63:08|The final and highest-scoring solution (`solution_final`, equivalent to Iteration 10) achieves a validation accuracy of **75.77%** (Validation error: 0.2423). It leverages a ConvNeXt-Tiny backbone fine-tuned via an unnormalized visual-prototype logit adjustment.
64:d4|
65:85|### Architecture & Pipeline
66:32|- **Base Model**: `models.convnext_tiny` with `IMAGENET1K_V1` weights. The classification head (`model.classifier[2]`) is replaced with a linear layer spanning `NUM_CLASSES = 1010`.
67:46|- **Feature Engineering (Visual Similarities)**: Before training, a sub-sample of the training data (up to 30 images per class) is passed through the pretrained backbone in `eval` mode. Features are extracted at 4 distinct intermediate stages. The class-wise mean for each stage is computed, normalized, and used to calculate a pairwise cosine similarity matrix. These 4 matrices are averaged and clamped `[0, 1]` to form a unified visual similarity matrix `V`.
68:9f|- **Training Setup**: AdamW optimizer (`lr=5e-4`, `weight_decay=1e-4`) with a CosineAnnealingLR scheduler over 7 epochs. Images are transformed via `RandomResizedCrop(224)` and `RandomHorizontalFlip`. The process relies on PyTorch AMP (Automatic Mixed Precision).
69:ed|- **Logit Adjustment**: The computed similarity matrix `V` is scaled by `beta=1.0` to form margin matrix `M`. The diagonal is set to 0. During the forward pass, `M[labels]` is directly added to the network logits before applying CrossEntropy loss (with `label_smoothing=0.1`).
70:98|- **Inference**: Uses `Resize(256)` and `CenterCrop(224)`. Generates Top-5 predictions per image to build the Kaggle-compliant `submission.csv`.
71:d4|
72:ac|### Code Snippets
73:d4|
74:7b|**1. Multi-Stage Feature Extraction**
75:12|```python
76:b2|class MultiStageModel(nn.Module):
77:90|    def __init__(self, base_model):
78:58|        super().__init__()
79:09|        self.features = base_model.features
80:7b|        
81:dd|    def forward(self, x):
82:54|        outputs = []
83:b5|        for i, layer in enumerate(self.features):
84:0d|            x = layer(x)
85:4a|            if i in [1, 3, 5, 7]:
86:a1|                outputs.append(F.adaptive_avg_pool2d(x, (1, 1)).flatten(1))
87:9f|        return outputs
88:30|```
89:23|*Caption: Extracts intermediate features from ConvNeXt-Tiny at 4 distinct layers to build multi-scale class prototypes for zero-cost visual similarity measurement.*
90:d4|
91:f3|**2. Zero-Cost Prototype and Similarity Matrix Computation**
92:12|```python
93:b0|extractor = MultiStageModel(model).cuda().eval()
94:4d|sum_features = {stage: torch.zeros(NUM_CLASSES, dim).cuda() for stage, dim in enumerate([96, 192, 384, 768])}
95:38|counts = torch.zeros(NUM_CLASSES).cuda()
96:d4|
97:f9|with torch.no_grad():
98:c1|    for images, labels in loader:
99:38|        images, labels = images.cuda(), labels.cuda()
100:80|        with torch.amp.autocast('cuda'):
101:ba|            feats = extractor(images)
102:00|        for stage, feat in enumerate(feats):
103:84|            sum_features[stage].index_add_(0, labels, feat.float())
104:8b|        counts.index_add_(0, labels, torch.ones_like(labels).float())
105:7b|        
106:88|V = np.zeros((NUM_CLASSES, NUM_CLASSES))
107:5b|for stage in range(4):
108:19|    mean_feat = sum_features[stage] / counts.unsqueeze(1).clamp(min=1)
109:9d|    mean_feat = F.normalize(mean_feat, p=2, dim=1).cpu().numpy()
110:55|    sim = mean_feat @ mean_feat.T
111:bf|    V += np.clip(sim, 0, 1)
112:d2|V /= 4
113:30|```
114:1f|*Caption: Aggregates and normalizes multi-layer prototypes efficiently via index addition, producing an average cosine similarity matrix robust to layer scale differences.*
115:d4|
116:80|**3. Pairwise Logit Adjustment in the Training Loop**
117:12|```python
118:48|with torch.amp.autocast('cuda'):
119:8f|    logits = model(images)
120:03|    # Apply pairwise margin
121:d3|    margins = M_tensor[labels]
122:e2|    adjusted_logits = logits + margins
123:f4|    loss = F.cross_entropy(adjusted_logits, labels, label_smoothing=0.1)
124:30|```
125:86|*Caption: Dynamically applies a scaled pairwise similarity matrix `M` as class margins on network logits to structurally penalize fine-grained visual confusions.*
